libuv. We adopt a subset of their supported platforms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eStrategy\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-strategy\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Strategy\" href=\"#strategy\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThere are three support tiers:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTier 1\u003c/strong\u003e: These platforms represent the majority of Node.js users. The\nNode.js Build Working Group maintains infrastructure for full test coverage.\nTest failures on tier 1 platforms will block releases.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTier 2\u003c/strong\u003e: These platforms represent smaller segments of the Node.js user\nbase. The Node.js Build Working Group maintains infrastructure for full test\ncoverage. Test failures on tier 2 platforms will block releases.\nInfrastructure issues may delay the release of binaries for these platforms.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eExperimental\u003c/strong\u003e: May not compile or test suite may not pass. The core team\ndoes not create releases for these platforms. Test failures on experimental\nplatforms do not block releases. Contributions to improve support for these\nplatforms are welcome.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003ePlatforms may move between tiers between major release lines. The table below\nwill reflect those changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePlatform list\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-platform-list\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Platform list\" href=\"#platform-list\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNode.js compilation/execution support depends on operating system, architecture,\nand libc version. The table below lists the support tier for each supported\ncombination. A list of \u003ca href=\"#supported-toolchains\"\u003esupported compile toolchains\u003c/a\u003e is\nalso supplied for tier 1 platforms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFor production applications, run Node.js on supported platforms only.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNode.js does not support a platform version if a vendor has expired support\nfor it. In other words, Node.js does not support running on End-of-Life (EoL)\nplatforms. This is true regardless of entries in the table below.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eOperating System\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eArchitectures\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eVersions\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eSupport Type\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eNotes\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eGNU/Linux\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ex64\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ekernel \u0026gt;= 4.18\u003csup\u003e\u003ca href=\"#user-content-fn-1-55dd82636bd220bcc30164207932caa4\" id=\"user-content-fnref-1-55dd82636bd220bcc30164207932caa4\" data-footnote-ref=\"\" aria-describedby=\"footnote-label\"\u003e1\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/sup\u003e, glibc \u0026gt;= 2.28\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eTier 1\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ee.g. Ubuntu 20.04, Debian 10, RHEL 8\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eGNU/Linux\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ex64\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ekernel \u0026gt;= 3.10, musl \u0026gt;= It will lint JavaScript, C++, and Markdown files.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo fix auto fixable JavaScript linting errors, use \u003ccode\u003emake lint-js-fix\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIf you are updating tests and want to run tests in a single test file\n(e.g. dir=\"auto\"\u003eIf you run into an issue where the information provided by the JS stack trace\nis not enough, or if you suspect the error happens outside of the JS VM, you\ncan try to build a debug enabled binary:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"./configure The\n\u003ccode\u003edistclean\u003c/code\u003e recipe aggressively removes build artifacts. You will need to\nbuild again (\u003ccode\u003emake -j4\u003c/code\u003e). Since all build artifacts have been removed, this\nrebuild may take a lot more time than previous builds. Additionally,\n\u003ccode\u003edistclean\u003c/code\u003e removes the file that stores the results of \u003ccode\u003e./configure\u003c/code\u003e. dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen building Node.js, provide a path to your ccache via the option:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-powershell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\".\\vcbuild.bat ccache c:\\ccache\\\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e.\\\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003evcbuild.bat\u003c/span\u003e ccache 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBy default Node.js is built so that all dependencies are bundled into\nthe Node.js binary itself. This provides a single binary that includes\nthe correct versions of all dependencies on which it depends.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSome Node.js distributions, however, prefer to manage dependencies.\nA number of \u003ccode\u003econfigure\u003c/code\u003e options are provided to support this use case.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor dependencies with native code, the first set of options allow\nNode.js to be built so that it uses a shared library\nat runtime instead of building and including the dependency\nin the Node.js binary itself. These options are in the\n\u003ccode\u003eShared libraries\u003c/code\u003e section of the \u003ccode\u003econfigure\u003c/code\u003e help\n(run \u003ccode\u003e./configure --help\u003c/code\u003e to get the complete list).\nThey provide the ability to enable the use of a shared library,\nto set the name of the shared library, and to set the paths that\ncontain the include and shared library files.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor dependencies with JavaScript code (including WASM), the second\nset of options allow the Node.js binary to be built so that it loads\nthe JavaScript for dependencies at runtime instead of being built into\nthe Node.js binary itself. These options are in the \u003ccode\u003eShared builtins\u003c/code\u003e\nsection of the \u003ccode\u003econfigure\u003c/code\u003e help\n(run \u003ccode\u003e./configure --help\u003c/code\u003e to get the complete list). They\nprovide the ability to set the path to an external JavaScript file\nfor the dependency to be used at runtime.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt is the responsibility of any distribution\nshipping with these options to:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eensure that the shared dependencies available at runtime\nmatch what is expected by the Node.js binary. A\nmismatch may result in crashes or unexpected behavior.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003efully test that Node.js operates as expected with the\nexternal dependencies. There may be little or no test coverage\nwithin the Node.js project CI for these non-default options.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote for downstream distributors of Node.js\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-note-for-downstream-distributors-of-nodejs\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Note for downstream distributors of Node.js\" href=\"#note-for-downstream-distributors-of-nodejs\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe Node.js ecosystem is reliant on ABI compatibility within a major release.\nTo maintain ABI compatibility it is required that distributed builds of Node.js\nbe built against the same version of dependencies, or similar versions that do\nnot break their ABI compatibility, as those released by Node.js for any given\n\u003ccode\u003eNODE_MODULE_VERSION\u003c/code\u003e (located in \u003ccode\u003esrc/node_version.h\u003c/code\u003e).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen Node.js is built (with an intention to distribute) with an ABI\nincompatible with the official Node.js builds (e.g. using a ABI incompatible\nversion of a dependency), please reserve and use a custom \u003ccode\u003eNODE_MODULE_VERSION\u003c/code\u003e\nby opening a pull request against the registry available at\n\u003ca href=\"https://github.com/nodejs/node/blob/HEAD/doc/abi_version_registry.json\"\u003ehttps://github.com/nodejs/node/blob/HEAD/doc/abi_version_registry.json\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003csection
